SUMMARY OF FINDINGS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
Our field exploration generally encountered a surface fill layer underlain by
soft loose lagoonal estuarine deposits to depths ranging between about 30 to 50 feet
below the existing ground surface Older alluvial materials consisting of very stiff clayey
silts and silty clays were then encountered to the maximum depth explored of
approximately 102 5 feet below the existing ground surface It should be noted that the
compressible lagoonal estuarine deposits encountered elsewhere appear to be absent in
Boring 106 and 107 The groundwater levels encountered generally
correspond to about Elevations 1 7 to 4 3 feet MSL
Based on the subsurface conditions encountered and the structural loads provided
we recommend utilizing 16 5 inch octagonal precast prestressed concrete piles to support
the proposed flood wall structure The driven piles will extend through the soft loose
lagoonal estuarine deposits and derive vertical support capacity from friction and end
bearing in the underlying very stiff alluvial clays The recommended pile lengths will need
to take into account of the expected downdrag loads resulting from the future embankment
fills placed across the project site Shorter pile lengths may be used along the last
300 feet of flood wall alignment towards Moanalua Freeway due to the substantial
reduction in the thickness of the lagoonal estuarine deposits
Based on the subsurface conditions encountered and the structural loads provided
we recommend utilizing 20 inch octagonal precast prestressed concrete piles to support
the proposed box culvert structure The driven piles will derive vertical support capacity
from friction and end bearing in the alluvial deposits consisting of medium dense silty
sands and very stiff clayey soils It should be noted that the compressible lagoonal or
estuarine deposits encountered elsewhere appear to be absent at the proposed box
culvert structure location
Because construction of the underground wet well structure will replace the soil with
lighter materials storm water runoff there is generally a net decrease in stresses on the
underlying soils Therefore we believe that a concrete mat may be used to provide the
necessary bearing support and uplift load resistance for the pump station structure Due to
the presence of very soft loose subsurface soils near the foundation subgrade level of the
underground wet well chambers we recommend providing a stabilization layer consisting
of 2 feet of No 2 Rock ASTM C 33 No 4 gradation wrapped in a woven geotextile
SUMMARY OF FINDINGS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page vii
Hawaii California
fabric such as Mirafi 500X or equivalent below the concrete mat for uniform bearing
support
A shallow foundation system consisting of mat footings may be used to support the
new generator building planned An allowable bearing pressure of up to may be
used for the design of shallow footings bearing on 2 feet of select granular fill material
compacted to a minimum of 95 percent relative compaction The 2 foot select granular fill
will serve to reduce the potential for adverse effects on the footing foundations resulting
from potential rise in flood water level to near the foundation subgrade level
Engineering analyses were performed to assess the slope stability of the earthen
levee and pile supported flood wall with sheet pile alternatives in general accordance
with the USACE s Chapter 6 of EM Design and Construction of Levees
and as required in FEMA Riverine Structures Form MT 2 Form 3 for
Levee and Floodwalls Based on our slope stability analyses the earthen levee structure
would not be stable during flooding and seismic events Therefore the earthen levee
alternative for flood mitigation was not pursued further for the project For the
pile supported flood wall with sheet pile alternative our slope stability analyses indicated
that the proposed structure would be stable under the different loading conditions for both
Phase II and Phase III development envisioned for the near term and long term flood
mitigation respectively
Seepage stability analyses were also performed for the Steady Seepage at Flood
Stage loading condition for the pile supported flood wall with sheet pile alternative Based
on our seepage analyses both the upward gradient and factor of safety satisfy the
minimum criteria presented in the publication entitled 569 Design Guidance
for Levee Underseepage suggesting that the potential for structure uplift and piping
should be minimal for the pile supported flood wall with sheet pile alternative
Based on the results of our engineering analyses it is our opinion that the
geotechnical design of the pile supported flood wall complies with the requirements of
Engineering Circular 6067
The text of this report should be referred to for detailed discussion and specific
design recommendations
END OF SUMMARY OF FINDINGS AND RECOMMENDATIONS

SECTION 1 GENERAL
This report presents the results of our geotechnical engineering evaluation
performed for the 56024 Flood Mitigation Structures project at Fort
Shafter Flats in Honolulu on the Island of Oahu Hawaii The project location and
general vicinity are shown on the Project Location Map Plate 1
This report summarizes the findings and geotechnical recommendations based
on our engineering analyses utilizing the information obtained from our literature review
past experience in the project vicinity and the geotechnical exploration conducted by
our office for the project The recommendations presented herein are intended for the
design and evaluation of foundations slabs on grade retaining structures sheet piling
slope stability seepage control site grading and utility installation only In addition
discussions on the excavation and dewatering requirements are included in this report
for information purposes The findings and recommendations presented herein are
subject to the limitations noted at the end of this report
1 1
Project Considerations
The Flood Mitigation Structures project is located at Fort Shafter Flats in
Honolulu on the Island of Oahu Hawaii The project involves the design of
levees floodwalls to reduce flooding caused by Kahauiki Stream when it overtops its
east bank and by interior drainage The flood mitigation project will allow the US Army to
move forward with 67188 67189 Tactical Equipment Maintenance
Facility TEMF and other future projects planned at Fort Shafter Flats
Based on the information provided the new structures and improvements
planned for this Phase II development include the following items A layout of the
proposed new construction is shown on the General Site Plan Plate 2
1
East Flood Levee Wall A new flood wall with steel sheet pile will be
installed along the makai side of Kahauiki Stream from about the existing
Kahauiki Makai Bridge to near Moanalua Freeway The flood wall will be
designed to provide a minimum freeboard of 3 feet above the 100 year flood
water surface elevation Due to the presence of underlying soft loose
subsoils we anticipate supporting the flood wall with driven pile foundation
SECTION 1 GENERAL
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 2
Hawaii California
Earthen levees were also considered for the project but deemed to be
unstable under flooding and earthquake loading conditions
2
Kahauiki Makai Culvert A new box culvert will be constructed west mauka
of the existing Kahauiki Makai Bridge to widen the existing drainage section
through this area Open channel retaining walls will also be required
upstream and downstream of the box culvert to allow expanded stream flow
3
Drainage Pump Station and Generator Building A new drainage pump
station and generator building are planned near the intersection of Stream
Road and Loop Road to handle the volume of water from a 10 year storm
The design finish floor elevation of the below grade portion of the pump
station building is set at about 10 0 feet Mean Sea Level MSL or
approximately 18 feet below the exterior finish grades The new generator
building will be a single story structure with slab on grade construction Pad
footing for the generator will be isolated from the perimeter walls to minimize
vibrations
4
Detention Basin A detention basin will be constructed between Loop Road
and Annex Road The detention basin will be about 7 feet high with
stabilized excavation slopes
5
New Sewer Line A new 18 inch sewer line is planned alongside the new
flood wall extending from about the existing Kahauiki Makai Bridge to the
northeastern corner of Building T 1522 The design pipe invert elevation of
the new sewer line will be at approximately 8 feet below the existing ground
surface at its deepest
6
New Drain Lines Various new drain lines are planned to collect and drain
surface runoff Additionally selected manholes will be raised above the flood
level
Under the future Phase III development plan the general site grades will be
raised above the flood level by placing about 6 to 8 feet of new imported fills Due to
the presence of soft loose subsoils below the site significant settlements will occur as a
result of these new fills Although this filling will be designed under a future contract
general recommendations cautions are included in our study
Important geotechnical considerations for the project include the following
Flood wall foundations The flood wall foundations will have to resist water
pressures as well as seepage forces below the wall and downdrag loads
from future fills Engineering analyses will be performed to evaluate the
slope stability and seepage control for the pile supported flood wall with
sheet pile design

Hawaii California
Foundation support of the new box culvert The subsurface conditions below
the new box culvert may vary from soft clays to stiff alluvium Proper
foundation support is needed to reduce the potential for differential
settlements
Foundation support of the new pump station The use of concrete mat
foundation to provide the necessary bearing support and uplift load
resistance for the underground wet well chambers will be evaluated
Foundation support of the new channel retaining walls Special attention will
be given to the foundation bearing materials along the upstream and
downstream ends of the new box culvert
Bearing support of the new sewer and drain lines Provision of a subgrade
stabilization layer underneath the new sewer and drain lines may be
required due to the potential presence of soft loose lagoonal estuarine
deposits at the pipe invert elevations
The detention basin construction will extend into the soft soils near the
groundwater table The excavated slopes may require stabilization erosion
protection

conditions at the site to develop an idealized soil rock data set to formulate geotechnical
recommendations for design of the flood mitigation structure project The scope of work
for this evaluation included the following tasks and work efforts
1
Research and review of available soils and boring data in the project
vicinity A list of the references used in the preparation of this report is
presented in the reference section

coordination of utility toning with the appropriate utility providers and
agencies
3
Preparation of a site specific Accident Prevention Plan APP and Activity
Hazard Analysis AHA
4
Mobilization and demobilization of a truck mounted drill rig and
two operators to the project site and back

SECTION 2 SITE CHARACTERIZATION
2 1
Regional Geology
The Island of Oahu is built by the extrusion of basaltic lavas from the Waianae
and Koolau shield volcanoes The older Waianae Volcano is estimated to be middle to
late Pliocene in age and forms the bulk of the western one third of the island The
younger Koolau Volcano is estimated to be late Pliocene to early Pleistocene Ice Age
in age and forms the majority of the eastern two thirds of the island The
Koolau Volcano reached the end of its main shield building phase about 2 million years
ago
The Koolau volcanic shield was built during the early Pleistocene Epoch by
thinly bedded basaltic lava flows The main shield building activities ceased
approximately 2 5 million years ago Evidence from drilled wells indicates that the island
of Oahu has subsided by as much as 1 200 feet since the cessation of this early
volcanic activity Macdonald and Abbot 1970
During that period of subsidence coral algal reefs began to grow on the southern
coast of Oahu forming broad bays with barrier reefs across its mouth The growth of the
reefs essentially kept pace with the rate of subsidence A series of lagoons formed
behind the barrier reefs and both terrigenous and marine sediments accumulated in the
lagoons Macdonald and Abbott 1970
During the later Pleistocene Epoch Ice Age many sea level changes occurred
as a result of widespread glaciation in the continental areas of the world As the great
continental glaciers advanced the ocean level fell since less water was available to fill
the oceanic basins Conversely as the glaciers receded or melted global sea levels
rose because more water was available The land mass of Oahu remained essentially
stable during these changes and the fluctuations were eustatic in nature These
glacio eustatic fluctuations resulted in stands of the sea which were both higher and
lower relative to the present sea level of Oahu
The higher sea level stands caused the accumulation of deltas and fans of
terrigenous sediments in the heads of old bays accumulation of reef deposits at
SECTION 2 SITE CHARACTERIZATION
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 7
Hawaii California
correspondingly higher elevations and deposition of lagoonal marine sediments in the
quiet waters protected by fringing reefs The lower sea stands caused streams to carve
valleys in the sediments and reef deposits Subaerial exposure of the sediments and
calcareous materials caused desiccation of the soft deltaic materials and lagoonal
deposits and induration of the calcareous reef materials In addition renewed subaerial
erosion of the upper areas of the volcanic dome deposited terrigenous alluvial soils
under relatively high energy conditions
During periods of no significant sea level changes continued stream action
extended the alluvial deltas and fans seaward and deposited alluvium over the lagoonal
sediments During these stable periods the growth of fringing coral algal reefs formed
distinct ledges of reef limestone at elevations roughly conforming to the level of the sea
during that period About 15 000 years ago a relatively rapid rise in sea level occurred
During that rise the valleys in the project area were submerged In the last
10 000 years or so the sea level has adjusted to its present stand Terrigenous and
marine sediments have continued to accumulate in low energy estuarine or lagoonal
environments resulting in thick deposits of soft loose sediments along the coast in areas
that were formerly valleys and drainageways In more recent time the efforts of man
have shaped the low lying land to its present form by placement of fill in low areas
Review of available geological information pertaining to the site and our current
exploration indicate that the site geology is highly complex reflecting past changes of
sea level post erosional volcanism and shifting of the courses of Moanalua Kahauiki
and Kalihi Streams as a result of the volcanic activity and alluviation at the head of
Keehi Lagoon The relevant sea level changes are indicated in the following table

Moanalua and Kahauiki Streams formerly flowed through the current location of
the Salt Lake and Aliamanu tuff cones members of the Honolulu Volcanic Series and
these streams were first dammed and then diverted by the deposition of the cones It
also appears that a significant amount of cinder from the Kalihi and Kamanaiki cinder
cone members accumulated in the floors of Moanalua and Kahauiki Valleys
Kalihi Stream was diverted to the western side of Kalihi Valley by lava flows from the
Kamanaiki cone
Geological evidence indicates that these members of the Honolulu Volcanic
Series erupted during the Waipio low stand of the sea 60 feet MSL about 0 5 million
years ago At some point after the damming of Moanalua and Kahauiki Streams the
volcanic deposits were breached and the streams diverted to the southeast to join Kalihi
Stream and form the head of Keehi Lagoon
The higher Waimanalo 25 feet MSL and stands of the sea
allowed for deposition of sediments derived from the cinder deposits at elevations
above current sea level and for depositions of beach deposits at the top of the slopes
adjacent to the site
The Mamala stand created a very deep base level which scoured portions of the
area including Keehi Lagoon to over 300 feet below existing sea level Rising sea level
resulted in the deposition of soft sediments within the scoured areas
2 2
Existing Site Conditions
The site is in the Fort Shafter Flats area within Fort Shafter in Honolulu on the
Island of Oahu Hawaii The site borders along Kahauiki Stream which runs from north
near the Moanalua Freeway to south near Building 1585 and includes much of the low
lying area to the east of the stream
Immediately adjacent to Kahauiki Stream the land is predominantly open lawn
area which at the time of our exploration was covered with sparse grass and scattered
landscaping trees The remainder of the site bounded generally by Takata Road
Suehiro Road and Signal Street consists mostly of paved yard area and is occupied by
various military structures including Buildings T 1507 the former location of T 1572
SECTION 2 SITE CHARACTERIZATION
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 9
Hawaii California
1578 and 1528 Building T 1507 and the remnant slab of Building T 1572 show
considerable deflection as a result of differential settlement
2 3
Subsurface Conditions
As previously mentioned the project site has been explored by PGE in 2007 and
2009 and by Geolabs in 2010 Our field exploration consisted of drilling and sampling
25 borings designated as Boring Nos 101 through 129 excluding and
113 extending to depths of about 16 5 to 102 5 feet below the existing ground surface
The approximate boring locations are shown on the Boring Location Plan Plate 3
Detailed boring locations are presented on the Site Plans Plates 4 1 through 4 4
Throughout most of the site our field exploration generally encountered a
surface layer of fills averaging about 10 feet in thickness underlain by soft lagoonal or
estuarine deposits to depths ranging between about 30 to 50 feet where older alluvial
materials consisting of very stiff gray and brown clayey silts and silty clays were
encountered to the maximum depth explored of 102 5 feet below the existing ground
surface In Boring 106 and 107 the lagoonal deposits were absent and
alluvial deposits derived from the Honolulu Volcanic Series cinder were encountered
under the man made fill
The fill materials generally consisted of dense to medium dense gravelly sands
and medium stiff to very stiff clayey silts extending down to about 10 to 15 feet below
the ground surface Some localized pockets of medium dense silty sands and sandy
gravels were also encountered within the fill layer As described above the fill materials
were generally underlain by lagoonal or estuarine deposits consisting of soft silts and
very loose silty gravels In the deeper borings along Kahauiki Stream cinder derived
alluvial deposits were encountered to depths of about 30 to 45 feet below the existing

Seismic Design Considerations
Based on the International Building Code 2009 Edition IBC 2009 the project
site may be subject to seismic activity and seismic design considerations will need to be
addressed The following subsections provide discussions on the seismicity soil profile
type for seismic design and the potential for liquefaction at the project site
Earthquakes and Seismicity
In general earthquakes throughout the world are caused by shifts in the tectonic
plates In contrast earthquake activity in Hawaii is linked primarily to volcanic
activity therefore earthquake activity in Hawaii generally occurs before or during
volcanic eruptions In addition earthquakes may result from the underground
SECTION 2 SITE CHARACTERIZATION
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 15
Hawaii California
movement of magma that comes close to the surface but does not erupt The
Island of Hawaii experiences thousands of earthquakes each year but most are so
small that they can be detected only by sensitive instruments However some of
the earthquakes are strong enough to be felt and a few cause minor to moderate
damage
In general earthquakes associated with volcanic activity are most common on the
Island of Hawaii Earthquakes that are directly associated with the movement of
magma are concentrated beneath the active Kilauea and Mauna Loa Volcanoes on
the Island of Hawaii Because majority of the earthquakes in Hawaii
over 90 percent are related to volcanic activity the risk of seismic activity and
degree of ground shaking diminishes with increased distance from the Island of
Hawaii The Island of Hawaii has experienced numerous earthquakes greater than
Magnitude 5 M5 however earthquakes are not confined only to the Island of
Hawaii
To a lesser degree the Island of Maui has experienced several earthquakes
greater than Magnitude 5 Therefore moderate to strong earthquakes have
occurred in the County of Maui The effects of earthquakes occurring on the Islands
of Hawaii and Maui may be felt on the Island of Oahu For example small
landslides occurred on the Island of Oahu as a result of the Maui Earthquake of
Some houses on the Island of Oahu were reportedly damaged as a
result of the Lanai Earthquake of 1871 M7
In the last 150 years of recorded history we are not aware of earthquakes greater
than Magnitude 6 that have occurred on the Island of Oahu An earthquake of
Magnitude 4 8 to 5 0 occurred along the Diamond Head Fault in 1948 on the Island
of Oahu The moderate tremor resulted in broken store windows ruptured building
walls and broken underground water mains

As previously mentioned the project site is generally blanketed by a surface fill
layer overlying soft loose compressible lagoonal or estuarine deposits over the

Hawaii California
majority of the project site and underlain by very stiff alluvial clays extending to
depths of over 100 feet below the existing ground surface

standpoint as a Soft Soil Profile Therefore we believe seismic design of the flood
wall channel retaining walls drainage pump station and generator building may be
based on a Site Class E soil profile in accordance with the International Building
Code Table No 2009 Edition Based on Site Class E the following
seismic design parameters were estimated and may be used for the seismic
analysis

Liquefaction Potential
Based on the International Building Code 2009 Edition the project site should be
evaluated for the potential for soil liquefaction Based on the subsurface conditions
encountered and a design peak ground acceleration of 0 294g liquefaction may
occur resulting in appreciable settlements at the ground surface Therefore the
potential effects of liquefaction should be taken into consideration in the design of
the proposed development
Soil liquefaction is a condition where saturated cohesionless soils located near the
ground surface undergo a substantial loss of strength due to the build up of excess
pore water pressures resulting from cyclic stress applications induced by
earthquakes In this process when the loose saturated sand deposit is subjected to
vibration such as during an earthquake the soil tends to densify and decrease in
volume causing an increase in pore water pressure If drainage is unable to occur
rapidly enough to dissipate the build up of pore water pressure the effective stress
internal strength of the soil is reduced Under sustained vibrations the pore water
pressure build up could equal the overburden pressure essentially reducing the
soil shear strength to zero and causing it to behave as a viscous fluid During
SECTION 2 SITE CHARACTERIZATION
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 18
Hawaii California
liquefaction the soil acquires a mobility sufficient to permit both horizontal and
vertical movements and if not confined will result in significant deformations
Soils most susceptible to liquefaction are loose uniformly graded fine grained
sands and loose silts with little cohesion The major factors affecting the liquefaction
characteristics of a soil deposit are as follows
FACTORS
LIQUEFACTION SUSCEPTIBILITY
Grain Size Distribution
Fine and uniform sands and silts are
more susceptible to liquefaction than
coarse or well graded sands
Initial Relative Density
Loose sands and silts are most
susceptible to liquefaction Liquefaction
potential is inversely proportional to
relative density
Magnitude and Duration of Vibration
Liquefaction potential is directly
proportional to the magnitude and
duration of the earthquake
In general the subsurface information obtained from the borings indicates that the
site is underlain by soft loose lagoonal or estuarine deposits overlying very stiff
alluvial deposits at greater depths The lagoonal estuarine deposits consisting of
loose silty sands and soft sandy silts with little cohesion are potentially liquefiable
during a seismic event of Magnitude 6 with an associated peak ground acceleration
of 0 294g
We evaluated the liquefaction potential of the saturated granular soils at the site
using the computer software program LiquefyPro Version 5 by CivilTech Software
and the procedures outlined by Youd et al 2001 Our analyses were performed
on selected borings based on a seismic event of Magnitude 6 with an associated
peak ground acceleration of 0 294g Results of our liquefaction analyses are
presented on Plates C 1 through C 4 in Appendix C
Based on our analyses it appears that some of the soft loose lagoonal estuarine
deposits below the surface fill have a factor of safety of less than 1 0 against
liquefaction Therefore it is our opinion that the project site could be subjected to
SECTION 2 SITE CHARACTERIZATION
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 19
Hawaii California
appreciable ground settlements up to about 13 inches in the event of liquefaction
during a moderate earthquake M6 However we believe that lateral spreading
associated with liquefaction would not be a significant design consideration based
on the relatively flat site topography

SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
Throughout most of the site our field exploration generally encountered a
surface layer of fills averaging about 10 feet thick underlain by soft loose lagoonal or
estuarine deposits to depths ranging between about 30 to 50 feet where older alluvial
materials consisting of very stiff gray and brown clayey silts and silty clays were
encountered to the maximum depth explored of 102 5 feet below the existing ground
surface In Boring 106 and 107 the lagoonal deposits were absent and
alluvial deposits derived from the Honolulu Volcanic Series cinder were encountered
under the man made fill The groundwater levels encountered generally correspond to
Elevations 1 7 to 4 3 feet MSL
Our engineering analyses suggest that some of the soft loose lagoonal estuarine
deposits below the surface fill have a factor of safety of less than 1 0 against
liquefaction Therefore it is our opinion that the project site could be subjected to
appreciable ground settlements up to about 13 inches in the event of liquefaction
during a moderate earthquake M6 However we believe that lateral spreading
associated with liquefaction would not be a significant design consideration based on
the relatively flat site topography
Based on the subsurface conditions encountered and the structural loads
provided by the project structural engineer we recommend utilizing deep foundations
consisting of 16 5 inch octagonal precast prestressed concrete piles to support the
proposed flood wall structure The driven piles will extend through the soft loose
lagoonal estuarine deposits and derive vertical support capacity from friction and end
bearing in the underlying very stiff alluvial clays starting at depths of about 40 feet below
the existing ground surface Due to the placement of future embankment fills across the
project site settlement of the soft loose lagoonal estuarine deposits will result in
downdrag loading of the deep foundations extending through the upper existing fills and
underlying compressible lagoonal estuarine deposits Therefore the recommended pile
lengths will need to take into account of the expected downdrag loads in the pile
foundation analyses Due to the substantial reduction in the thickness of the
lagoonal estuarine deposits along the last 300 feet of flood wall alignment towards
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 21
Hawaii California
Moanalua Freeway we believe that shorter pile lengths may be used along this section
of the flood wall alignment Due to the substantial length of the near 100 foot long piles
for the flood wall structure we recommend that splicing of shorter pile sections be used
to extend the driven piles down to the estimated pile tip elevation to achieve the design
pile capacity
Based on the subsurface conditions encountered and the structural loads
provided by the project structural engineer we recommend utilizing deep foundations
consisting of 20 inch octagonal precast prestressed concrete piles to support the
proposed box culvert structure The driven piles will derive vertical support capacity
from friction and end bearing in the alluvial deposits consisting of medium dense silty
sands and very stiff clayey soils It should be noted that the compressible lagoonal or
estuarine deposits encountered elsewhere appear to be absent at the proposed box
culvert structure location
Because construction of the underground wet well chambers will replace the soil
with lighter materials storm water runoff there is generally a net decrease in stresses
on the underlying soils On this basis we believe that a concrete mat may be used to
provide the necessary bearing support and uplift load resistance for the pump station
structure Due to the presence of very soft loose subsurface soils near the foundation
subgrade level of the underground wet well chambers we recommend providing a
stabilization layer consisting of 2 feet of No 2 Rock ASTM C 33 No 4 gradation
wrapped in a woven geotextile fabric such as Mirafi 500X or equivalent below the
concrete mat for uniform bearing support
We believe a shallow foundation system consisting of mat footings may be used to
support the new generator building planned An allowable bearing pressure of up to
3 000 pounds per square foot psf may be used for the design of shallow footings bearing
on 2 feet of select granular fill material compacted to a minimum of 95 percent relative
compaction The 2 foot select granular fill will serve to reduce the potential for adverse
effects on the footing foundations resulting from potential rise in flood water level to near
the foundation subgrade level In general the bottom of footings should be embedded a
minimum of 18 inches below the lowest adjacent finished grade

Page 22
Hawaii California
We have performed engineering analyses to assess the slope stability of the
earthen levee and pile supported flood wall with sheet pile alternatives in general
accordance with the USACE s Chapter 6 of EM Design and Construction of
Levees and as required in FEMA Riverine Structures Form MT 2 Form 3
for Levee and Floodwalls Based on our slope stability analyses for the earthen levee
alternative the factor of safety under Case IV Steady Seepage at Flood Stage and
Case VI Earthquake loading conditions did not meet the minimum requirement of 1 4 and
1 0 respectively indicating that the earthen levee structure would not be stable during
flooding and seismic events Therefore the earthen levee alternative for flood mitigation
was not pursued further for the project For the pile supported flood wall with sheet pile
alternative our slope stability analyses indicate that the proposed structure would be
stable under the different loading conditions for both Phase II and Phase III development
envisioned for the near term and long term flood mitigation respectively
Seepage stability analyses were performed for the Steady Seepage at Flood Stage
loading condition for the pile supported flood wall with sheet pile alternative Based on our
seepage analyses both the upward gradient and factor of safety satisfy the minimum
criteria presented in the publication entitled 569 Design Guidance for Levee
Underseepage suggesting that the potential for structure uplift and piping should be
minimal for the pile supported flood wall with sheet pile alternative Detailed discussions
and specific recommendations for design of foundations slabs on grade retaining
structures sheet piling slope stability seepage control site grading utility installation and
other geotechnical aspects of the project are presented in the following sections

about the existing Kahauiki Makai Bridge to near Moanalua Freeway The flood wall will
be designed with top of wall elevation at about 16 feet MSL or about 3 feet above the
flood level of 13 feet MSL

provided by the project structural engineer we recommend utilizing deep foundations
consisting of 16 5 inch octagonal precast prestressed concrete piles to support the

proposed flood wall structure The driven piles will extend through the soft loose

Based on the information provided the proposed pile layout will consist of 2 pile

the wall alignment extending from 14 to An estimated pile length

Downdrag Loads
New fills needed to raise the site to the finished grades will induce ground
settlements as a result of consolidation of the underlying compressible
lagoonal estuarine deposits When the soft loose lagoonal estuarine deposits move
downward relative to the pile the downward movement will result in negative skin
friction forces generally known as downdrag forces acting on the pile shaft The
magnitude of the downdrag force depends on the thickness of the compressible
layer consistency relative density of the compressible lagoonal estuarine deposits
and the pile perimeter
Based on the long term flood mitigation plan for Fort Shafter Flats we understand
that the project site will be raised above the existing ground by placing about 6 to
8 feet of embankment fills in the future Due to the placement of future
embankment fills across the project site settlement of the soft loose
lagoonal estuarine deposits will result in downdrag loading of the deep foundations
extending through the upper existing fills and underlying compressible
lagoonal estuarine deposits Therefore the expected downdrag loads will need to
be accounted for in the pile foundation analyses Based on our foundation
analyses we estimate that the downdrag loads imposed on the vertical piles due to
the placement of the future fills may be on the order of about 78 5 kips per pile
proposed pile lengths presented above have already taken into account these
future downdrag loads
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 26
Hawaii California
Consideration has been given to the use of bitumen coating to reduce the
downdrag loads on the driven piles Because of the variable thickness of the
compressible deposits ranging from about 7 to 40 feet it would be very difficult to
determine the downdrag zones for bitumen coating application along the flood wall
alignment Application of bitumen coating below the downdrag zones would
actually reduce the load carrying contribution of the underlying alluvial deposits In
addition there exist the potential for damaging the bitumen coating during handling
and pile driving and environmental concerns such as contamination of
groundwater etc Therefore we believe that increasing the pile length would be a
more prudent approach in handling the downdrag loads on the driven pile
foundations
In addition to the downdrag forces acting on the pile shaft as discussed above the
wall footing will also experience downdrag load applied along the plane extending
vertically from the heel of the footing This downdrag load is caused by the relative
movement between the rigid block of soil above the wall footing and the adjacent
downward moving soils resulting from the future fill placement Based on our
engineering analyses this downdrag load acting on the wall footing is on the order
of about 675 pounds per lineal foot The maximum axial loads provided by the
project structural engineer have already taken into account of this downdrag load
Lateral Load Resistance
Lateral loads imposed on the flood wall structure may be resisted by the lateral load
capacity of the driven piles Lateral load resistance of driven piles is a function of
the stiffness of the surrounding soil the stiffness of the pile allowable deflection at
the top of the pile and the induced moment in the pile In general we recommend
spacing the driven piles a minimum of 2 5 times the diameter of the pile from
center to center Therefore the effect of group action was considered in our lateral
load analyses by including an efficiency factor in the direction of loading
The lateral load analyses were performed using the program GROUP 8 0 for
Windows which is a microcomputer adaptation of a finite difference laterally
loaded driven pile program originally developed at the University of Texas at Austin
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 27
Hawaii California
The program solves for deflection and bending moment along a driven pile under
lateral loads as a function of depth The analysis was carried out with the use of
non linear p y curves to represent soil moduli The lateral deflection was then
computed using the appropriate soil moduli at various depths
Based on the lateral load demand provided by the project structural engineer the
associated horizontal deflection and maximum induced moment for the driven piles
where the tops of piles are either free or fixed against rotation are presented in the
following table

Kahauiki Makai Culvert
A new box culvert will be installed west mauka of the existing Kahauiki Makai
Bridge to widen the existing drainage section through this area Open channel retaining
walls will be required upstream and downstream of the box culvert to allow expanded
stream flow
Based on the subsurface conditions encountered and the structural loads
provided by the project structural engineer we recommend utilizing deep foundations
consisting of 20 inch octagonal precast prestressed concrete piles to support the
proposed box culvert structure The driven piles will derive vertical support capacity
from friction and end bearing in the alluvial deposits consisting of medium dense silty
sands and very stiff clayey soils

Thrust Blocks for Water Lines
Based on the information provided we understand that concrete piles are
required at the six thrust blocks for the 8 and 12 inch water lines at the west end of the
new box culvert and at the east abutment of the existing Kahauiki Makai Bridge Each
thrust block will require one pile subjected to 45 kips in compression and 27 kips in

prestressed concrete piles to support the proposed thrust blocks for the water lines An
estimated pile tip elevation of 39 feet MSL may be used for preliminary design and cost
estimation purposes
3 4
Driven Pile Foundations
As previously mentioned we envision that driven pile foundations will be used for
support of the proposed flood wall box culvert and thrust blocks planned for the flood
mitigation project The following subsections provide further discussions on some of the
design and construction issues for the driven pile foundations
Predrilling
To facilitate seating of the pile segment and driving through the upper fill crust we
recommend that predrilling to a depth of 5 feet below the ground surface be
implemented for the driven piles planned for the East Flood Levee Wall In
addition the predrilling depth should be increased to a depth of 10 feet for those
concrete piles that are in proximity to existing structures and utilities to reduce the
potential for disturbance from vibrations generated during the pile driving operation
The predrilled holes should have a diameter of approximately 20 inches for the
16 5 inch octagonal piles and 24 inches for the 20 inch octagonal piles The
annular space between the piles and predrilled holes should be backfilled with pea
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 30
Hawaii California
gravel S4C sand or grouted with tremie concrete to fill in the voids where
appropriate The required predrilling size and depth should be verified and or
modified by Geolabs during the test pile driving operation depending on the cast
length conditions encountered and pile driving equipment used
Foundation Settlements
Settlement of the pile foundations will result from elastic compression of the pile
member and subgrade response of the foundation embedded in the
lagoonal estuarine deposits and alluvium underlying the project site Total
settlements of the pile supported foundation under the design loads are estimated
to be on the order of less than 0 75 inches Differential settlements between
adjacent piles should not exceed about one half of the total foundation settlement
We believe that a significant portion of the settlement is elastic and should occur as
the loads are applied
Pile Hammer Selection
In general we recommend driving the piles with a hammer capable of delivering a
minimum rated energy of 40 000 foot pounds in the field The hammer should be
equipped with an energy level control such that driving within the soft and or loose
soils may be controlled at a lower energy to reduce the potential for tensile stress
development which could damage or cause cracking of the piles
Selection of driving equipment to be used for this project should take into
consideration the matching of the pile hammer with the weight of the piles to be
driven This will result in the pile hammer efficiently delivering the required energy
to the top of the pile and also reducing the potential for damage to the piles
Geolabs should review the pile driving equipment proposed to evaluate whether the
equipment is capable of installing the piles to the recommended capacity The
contractor should forward pile and driving equipment data forms to Geolabs prior to
construction for evaluation and acceptance
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 31
Hawaii California
Pile Driving Criteria
For preliminary design of the 16 5 inch octagonal precast prestressed concrete
piles for the flood wall structure pile driving may be terminated when the driven pile
has achieved the minimum embedment depths into the very stiff older alluvial
deposit presented above or the blow counts steadily increase with depth and reach
5 blows per inch for the last 6 inches or when aggregated blow counts are
60 blows for the last foot For preliminary design of the 20 inch octagonal precast
prestressed concrete piles for the new box culvert pile driving may be terminated
when the driven pile has reached its design pile tip elevation or the blow counts
steadily increase with depth and reach 5 blows per inch for the last 6 inches or
when aggregated blow counts are 60 blows for the last foot The preliminary
driving criteria should be confirmed and or modified after selection of the pile driving
equipment and performance of a wave equation analysis
Each pile should be driven continuously without interruption A pile may be rejected
or its design capacity may be reduced when the driving resistance is interrupted for
more than 4 hours and the pile cannot be driven to the required depth During soft
driving such as when the pile tip is within soft loose soils the hammer stroke
or energy should be carefully controlled such that significant tensile stresses do
not develop within the pile
Because variations in soil strength characteristics are likely to exist in the bearing
soils the supporting capacity of each pile should be confirmed in the field by a
Geolabs representative during driving It should be noted that the pile design was
developed from our pile analysis using the field exploration data A test pile
program should be carried out to confirm our preliminary pile design and establish
the pile driving criteria The production pile driving criteria may be revised based on
the test pile program
Test Pile Program
Due to the variable thickness of the compressible deposits across the project site
we recommend conducting a test pile program which includes at least three static
load tests to fulfill the following objectives
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 32
Hawaii California
1
To examine the drivability of the piles with the use of the selected
hammer
2
To estimate the production pile lengths for the various structures
planned across the project site
3
To assess the test pile driving criteria which may be modified for
use as the production pile driving criteria
To achieve these objectives we recommend that the test pile program consist of a
minimum of 10 percent of the total number of piles for the project The test piles
may be incorporated into the actual foundation system upon the evaluation of the
pile driving behavior and the load test results When the final foundation plans are
available Geolabs should be consulted for selection of the test pile locations
In general the test piles should be cast at least 10 feet longer than the estimated
pile lengths to account for potential variations Splice cans should be made
available during the course of the test pile driving operations to allow for splicing of
the piles It should be noted that splice cans may be considered long lead items
because the splice cans are fabricated on the Mainland U S and shipped to
Hawaii
In addition the test pile program should provide some flexibility to allow for addition
and or relocation of the test piles as may be deemed necessary by our office to
suit the conditions encountered during the test pile driving Re striking of all the test
piles may be required as part of the test pile program
As previously mentioned a minimum of three static pile load tests should be
conducted on driven test piles selected by Geolabs based on field observations
during the test pile program The pile load tests should be performed in general
accordance with ASTM Test Designation D 1143 Standard Loading Procedure
loading the test pile to 200 percent of the anticipated design load For the 16 5 inch
octagonal load test pile between 14 and a design load of
180 kips should be used for the load test program For the 16 5 inch octagonal
load test pile between and a design load of 150 kips should
be used for the load test program For the 20 inch octagonal load test pile at the

Kahauiki Makai Culvert a design load of 136 kips should be used for the load test

3 5
Kahauiki Makai Bridge Foundations
As previously mentioned a non destructive testing survey was conducted by
Olson Engineering Inc in March 2011 to provide information about the integrity and
length of the concrete pile foundations supporting the abutments of the existing
Kahauiki Makai Bridge The test results indicated that the pile tips in the two stream
bents varied from about 57 to 79 feet below the bottom of the bridge deck which is at
an elevation of about 11 feet MSL Therefore it appears that the pile tip elevations of
the existing bridge foundation varied from about 48 to 70 feet MSL suggesting that the
driven piles were embedded into the stiff alluvial soils and well below the scour depth of
7 feet Based on our evaluation it is our opinion that the bridge pier bent piles could
each support a minimum axial load of 50 kips assuming a scour depth of not exceeding
14 feet below the mudline
3 6
Drainage Pump Station
Based on the information provided we understand that a new drainage pump
station is planned near the intersection of Stream Road and Loop Road to handle the
volume of water from a 10 year storm The design finish floor elevations for the
on grade pump room and below grade wet well of the new drainage pump station are
set at about 8 0 and 10 0 feet MSL respectively In addition we understand that the
underground wet well will be centered with the pump station building
Based on the preliminary drawings provided we anticipate that the bottom of the
underground wet well chambers may be embedded about 18 feet below the design
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 34
Hawaii California
finish grade Therefore installation of the underground wet well chambers will involve
an excavation of over 20 feet below the existing ground surface Because construction
of the underground structure will replace the soil with lighter materials storm water
runoff there is generally a net decrease in stresses on the underlying soils On this
basis we believe that a concrete mat may be used to provide the necessary bearing
support and uplift load resistance for the pump station structure A net allowable bearing
pressure of up to may be used to design the concrete mat bearing on a
stabilization layer as described below This allowable bearing pressure is for dead plus
live loads and may be increased by one third 1 3 for transient loads such as temporary
wind and or seismic forces
Due to the presence of very soft loose subsurface soils near the foundation
subgrade level of the underground wet well chambers we recommend providing a
stabilization layer consisting of 2 feet of No 2 Rock ASTM C 33 No 4 gradation
wrapped in a woven geotextile fabric such as Mirafi 500X or equivalent below the
concrete mat for uniform bearing support The woven geotextile fabric would serve as a
separation layer and provide additional strength to the underlying soft loose subgrade
In addition the stabilization layer would also serve as a working platform during
construction In order to reduce the potential for significant settlement of the
underground structure we recommend sewing in lieu of overlapping the woven
geotextile fabric and using light compaction equipment during installation of the
underground wet well chambers In addition the 2 foot thick stabilization layer should
extend a minimum of 2 feet beyond the edges of the concrete mat
Due to the shallow groundwater level anticipated at the project site the proposed
underground wet well chambers will be subjected to buoyant uplift forces Resistance to
uplift loads may be mobilized by the dead weight of the underground structure the
concrete mat and the backfill material above the concrete mat Contribution of dead
weight from the backfill may be estimated using a unit weight of 110 pounds per cubic
foot pcf above the groundwater table and 46 pcf below the groundwater table For side
shear between the structure and the backfill material a nominal value of 100 psf may be
used in design For evaluating uplift forces due to hydrostatic pressures we understand
that a high groundwater level of Elevation 7 feet MSL will be used for design
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 35
Hawaii California
Settlements of the new underground structure may result from compression of
the soft loose soil layer due to the placement of the backfill material and or disturbance
of the soft loose subsurface soils during construction We estimate the total settlement
of the underground structure to be on the order of about 1 to 2 inches We believe that
most more than one half of the settlements should occur during the construction
period
Because of the soft loose subsurface soils encountered some movement of soils
around the new underground wet well excavations should be anticipated due to
changes in the earth stresses during and after construction especially during extraction
of the sheet pile shoring system where provided Therefore we recommend
incorporating some flexibility in the connection of the piping network to the underground
chambers in the design to accommodate possible earth movements
Underground wet well chambers at the pump station building should be designed
to resist the lateral earth pressures due to the adjacent soil and surcharge effects The
lateral earth pressures acting on the underground wet well structure will depend on the
type of backfill used the extent of backfill and the compaction effort on the backfill
material around the structure For backfill below the groundwater table we anticipate
that it may be desirable to backfill behind the retaining structure using a free draining
type of backfill such as No 3B Fine gravel ASTM C 33 No 67 gradation or Crushed
Rock No 67 conforming to Section 15 of the City and County Standard Specifications
This is to reduce the compaction effort required and to facilitate backfill below the
groundwater table or in a wet environment If a free draining type of backfill is used a
filter fabric should be used to wrap around the free draining backfill In general the
lateral earth pressure design parameters presented in the Retaining Structures section
of this report may be used for the design of the underground wet well chambers at the
pump station building

Generator Building
Based on the subsurface conditions encountered at the project site we believe a
shallow foundation system consisting of mat footings may be used to support the new
generator building planned An allowable bearing pressure of up to may be

used for the design of shallow footings bearing on 2 feet of select granular fill material
compacted to a minimum of 95 percent relative compaction This bearing value is for
as those caused by wind or seismic forces The 2 foot select granular fill will serve to
reduce the potential for adverse effects on the footing foundations resulting from
potential rise in flood water level to near the foundation subgrade level
In general the bottom of footings should be embedded a minimum of 18 inches
below the lowest adjacent finished grade Foundations next to utility trenches and or
easements should be embedded below a 45 degree imaginary plane extending upward
from the bottom edge of the utility trench or embedded as deep as the inverts of the
utility lines This requirement is necessary to avoid surcharging adjacent below grade
structures with additional structural loads and to reduce the potential for appreciable
foundation settlement
The soils encountered at the bottom of the 2 foot thick select granular fill material
should be recompacted to a minimum of 90 percent relative compaction Soft and or
loose materials that are encountered at the bottom of the select granular fill material
should be over excavated to expose the underlying firm or dense materials The
over excavation should be backfilled with select granular fill material compacted to a
minimum of 95 percent relative compaction or the footings may be extended down to
the firm or dense materials
If the foundations are designed and constructed in accordance with our
recommendations we estimate that total settlements of footings bearing on the
recompacted in situ soils or new compacted fills may be on the order of about 1 inch or
less We estimate that differential settlements between adjacent footings supported on
similar materials to be on the order of about 0 5 inches
Lateral loads acting on the structure may be resisted by friction developed
between the bottom of the foundation and the bearing soil and by passive earth
pressure against the near vertical faces of the foundation system A coefficient of
friction of 0 4 may be used for footings bearing on the compacted select granular fill

Slabs On Grade
In general we envision that new slab on grade required will be supported on the
recompacted in situ soils or new compacted fills For interior building slabs not
subjected to vehicular traffic or equipment vibration we recommend placing a minimum
4 inch thick layer of cushion fill consisting of open graded gravel ASTM C 33 No 67
gradation below the slabs The open graded gravel cushion fill would serve as a
capillary moisture break and would provide more uniform support of the slabs To
reduce the potential for future moisture infiltration through the slab and subsequent
damage to floor coverings an impervious moisture barrier is recommended on top of
the open graded gravel cushion layer We also recommend that the interior wall design
incorporate some flexibility to accommodate a small amount of possible ground
movements
Where slabs will be subjected to vehicular traffic such as trucks and or forklifts
or equipment vibration we recommend providing a 6 inch layer of aggregate subbase
below the slabs in lieu of the 4 inch thick gravel cushion layer The moisture barrier
may be omitted for these slabs The aggregate subbase should consist of crushed
basaltic aggregates compacted to a minimum of 95 percent relative compaction For
the design of structural slabs supported on 6 inches of aggregate subbase a modulus
of subgrade reaction of about 250 pounds per square inch per inch of deflection pci
may be used for the compacted aggregate subbase Where slabs are intended to
function as rigid pavements for trucks a minimum slab thickness of 6 inches may be
used for preliminary design purposes Provisions should be made for proper load
transfer across the slab joints that will be subjected to vehicular traffic
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 38
Hawaii California
The thickened edges of slabs adjacent to unpaved areas should be embedded at
least 12 inches below the lowest adjacent grade It should be emphasized that the
areas adjacent to the slabs should be backfilled tightly against the edges of the slabs
with relatively impervious soils These areas should also be graded to divert water
away from the slabs and to reduce the potential for water ponding around the slabs

increased by up to one third 1 3 for transient loads such as those caused by wind or
seismic forces

subgrade level should be over excavated to expose the underlying firm or dense
materials The over excavation should be backfilled with select granular fill material
compacted to a minimum of 90 percent relative compaction or the footings may extend
down to bear on the firm or dense materials

3 10 Retaining Structures

Wall Foundations

retaining structures are presented in the respective sections herein In general we
envision that shallow foundations may be used to support the open channel walls
and the below grade portion of the pump station building while driven pile
foundations would be required for the support of the new flood wall and box culvert

Drainage
Retaining structures should be well drained to reduce the potential for build up of
hydrostatic pressures especially due to seepage water and or perched
groundwater A typical drainage system for basement walls would consist of a
minimum 12 inch wide zone of permeable material such as open graded gravel
ASTM C 33 No 67 gradation placed directly around a perforated pipe
perforations facing down at the base of the retaining wall The perforated pipe
should discharge to an appropriate outlet
As an alternative to the use of permeable material a prefabricated drainage
product such as MiraDrain 6200 or EnkaDrain may be used instead of the
permeable drainage material The prefabricated drainage product also should be
hydraulically connected to a perforated pipe at the base of the retaining wall The
perforated pipe should discharge to an appropriate outlet Unless covered by
concrete or asphaltic concrete the upper 12 inches of backfill above the
permeable drainage material and or prefabricated drainage product should consist
of relatively impervious materials to reduce the potential for significant surface
water infiltration behind the walls
For site retaining walls the typical drainage system may consist of 1 to 2 cubic foot
of permeable material such as open graded gravel ASTM C 33 No 67 gradation

wrapped with non woven filter fabric placed at each of the weep hole locations The
weep holes should be spaced no more than 6 to 8 feet apart
3 11 Steel Sheet Piling
Based on the information provided we understand that steel sheet pile walls will
be installed along a portion of the toe of the eastern levee stream bank for scour
protection Design of the sheet pile wall will need to consider both overturning stability
and overall slope stability Geotechnical design parameters to evaluate these stability
conditions are presented in the following subsections The overturning stability will
need to be evaluated by the design engineer We have evaluated the overall slope
stability for the proposed development and the results are presented in the Slope
Stability Analyses section of the report
The sheet pile wall at the toe of the eastern levee stream bank should be
designed to resist the lateral earth pressures due to the adjacent soils and surcharge
effects We recommend designing the sheet pile wall for lateral earth pressures due to
the in situ soils which generally consist of the soft lagoonal and estuarine deposits
Based on the anticipated subsurface conditions the recommended lateral earth
pressures for design of the sheet pile wall expressed as an equivalent fluid pressure in
pounds per square foot per foot of depth pcf are provided in the following table

3 12 Slope Stability Analyses
We have performed engineering analyses to assess the slope stability of the
earthen levee and pile supported flood wall with sheet pile alternatives in general
accordance with the USACE s Chapter 6 of EM Design and Construction
of Levees and as required in FEMA Riverine Structures Form MT 2
Form 3 for Levee and Floodwalls
The slope stability analyses were performed using the computer software
programs Slide 6 0 developed by Reoscience Slope stability analyses were performed
for both Phase II and Phase III development envisioned for the near term and long term
flood mitigation respectively Under Phase II development an earthen levee or pile
supported flood wall with sheet pile will be constructed for near term flood mitigation
purpose Under Phase III development the existing ground behind the earthen levee or
pile supported flood wall with sheet pile will be raised to a finish grade of about 16 feet
MSL with new embankment fills to provide long term flood mitigation
In accordance with FEMA Riverine Structures Form MT 2 Form 3 for Levee and

3 13 Seepage Analyses
When seepage occurs beneath concrete or other impermeable structures or
strata the underside of this impermeable barrier is subject to a force which tends to lift
the structure upward The determination of this pressure or force is important in
analyzing the stability of the structure According to the criteria presented in the
Engineering Technical Letters ETL published by the US Army Corps of Engineers
569 Design Guidance for Levee Underseepage 1 May 2005 the
maximum upward gradient and minimum factor of safety should be 0 3 and 3 0
respectively
We have performed engineering analyses to assess the seepage conditions of
the pile supported flood wall with sheet pile alternative as required in FEMA Riverine
Structures Form MT 2 Form 3 for Levee and Floodwalls The seepage analyses were
performed using the computer software program Slide 6 0 developed by Reoscience
Seepage stability analyses were performed for the loading condition Case IV Steady
Seepage at Flood Stage under both Phase II and Phase III site development

minimal for the pile supported flood wall with sheet pile alternative
3 14 Site Grading
Based on the existing topography and the anticipated finished grades for the
Phase II development we anticipate that the site grading work for the project
construction will consist of minor fills on the order of about 2 feet or less Substantial
excavations over 20 feet deep will be required for the construction of the below grade
portion of the pump station building The following grading items are addressed in the
succeeding subsections
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 49
Hawaii California
Site Preparation
Fill Materials
Fill Placement and Compaction Requirements
Cut and Fill Slopes
Filled Ground Settlement
Settlement Monitoring
Geolabs should monitor the earthwork operations to observe whether
undesirable materials are encountered during the excavation and filling process and to
confirm whether the exposed soil and or rock conditions are similar to those
encountered and assumed in the design
Site Preparation
At the on set of earthwork areas within the contract grading limits should be
cleared thoroughly Vegetation debris deleterious materials and other unsuitable
materials should be removed and disposed properly off site to reduce the potential
for contaminating the excavated materials to be used as fill backfill materials
Slabs and foundations of the existing structures and pavements to be demolished
should be completely removed Over excavations resulting from the demolition
operations should be backfilled with compacted granular fill material Existing
underground utilities to be abandoned should be removed and the resulting
excavation should be properly backfilled with the excavated on site materials The
on site materials should be moisture conditioned to above the optimum moisture
content placed in 6 to 8 inch level loose lifts and compacted to a minimum of
90 percent relative compaction Utilities to be abandoned in place under the
proposed structure should be backfilled by pumping lean concrete or CLSM
Controlled Low Strength Material under low pressure
After clearing and demolishing the excavated subgrades underneath future slab
and pavement areas should be scarified to a depth of about 8 inches
moisture conditioned to at least 2 percent above the optimum moisture content and
recompacted to a minimum of 90 and 95 percent relative compaction respectively
Where shrinkage cracks are observed after compaction of the subgrade we
recommend preparing the subgrade soil again as recommended above Saturation
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 50
Hawaii California
and subsequent yielding of the exposed subgrade due to inclement weather and
poor drainage may require over excavation of the soft areas and replacement with
well compacted fill The need for over excavation due to soft subgrade soil
conditions should be evaluated in the field by a Geolabs representative
Fill Materials
In general the excavated on site granular materials may be used as a source of fill
material provided that deleterious materials such as vegetation are removed and
over sized materials greater than 3 inches in maximum dimension are screened
Imported fill materials required for the project construction should consist of
non expansive select granular material such as crushed coral and basalt The
material should be well graded from coarse to fine with particles no larger than
3 inches in largest dimension and should contain between 10 and 30 percent
particles passing the No 200 sieve The material should have a laboratory CBR
value of 20 or more and should have a maximum swell of 1 percent or less when
tested in accordance with ASTM D 1883
Aggregate base course and aggregate subbase materials required for the project
should consist of crushed basaltic aggregates and should conform to Subsections
703 06 and 703 17 respectively of the State of Hawaii Standard Specifications for
Road and Bridge Construction 2005
