should test the imported fill materials for conformance with these recommendations
prior to delivery to the project site for the intended use
Fill Placement and Compaction Requirements
Select granular fill materials should be moisture conditioned to above the optimum
moisture placed in level lifts of about 8 inches in loose thickness and compacted
to at least 95 percent relative compaction Aggregate base course and subbase
materials should be moisture conditioned to above the optimum moisture content
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 51
Hawaii California
placed in level lifts not exceeding 8 inches in loose thickness and compacted to a
minimum of 95 percent relative compaction
Relative compaction refers to the in place dry density of soil expressed as a
percentage of the maximum dry density of the same soil established in accordance
with ASTM D 1557 Optimum moisture is the water content percentage by weight
corresponding to the maximum dry density Compaction should be accomplished
by sheepsfoot rollers vibratory rollers or other types of acceptable compaction
equipment
Cut and Fill Slopes
Permanent cut and fill slopes planned for the project should be constructed at an
inclination of 2H 1V or flatter Fills should be keyed and benched into the existing
slope to provide stability of the new fill against sliding The filling operations should
start at the lowest point and continue up in level horizontal compacted layers in
accordance with the fill placement recommendations presented above Excessive
surface water should be diverted away from the tops of slopes and slope planting
should be provided as soon as the fill slopes are completed to reduce the potential
for erosion of the finished slopes
Filled Ground Settlement
Based on the existing topography and design finish floor elevation for the pump
station and generator building we envision site filling on the order of about 1 5
feet thick will be required for the building construction Placement of new fills to
raise the site to the finished subgrade elevation likely will induce some ground
settlements as a result of consolidation of the underlying compressible deposits
Our engineering analyses suggest that settlements on the order of about 3 to
4 inches may be anticipated as a result of the consolidation of the compressible
deposits under the new fill loads To reduce the impact of the anticipated ground
settlements on the new construction caused by consolidation of the compressible
deposits under the new fill loads we recommend placing the new fills as soon as
practical at the commencement of the Phase II construction and delaying the
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 52
Hawaii California
generator building slab and pavement construction as late as practical to allow
the anticipated ground settlements to occur In addition we recommend that
flexible pipe joints be used to connect the piping to the new buildings to allow for
some amount of differential movement
Based on the information provided we understand that the existing ground at the
project site will be raised by about 6 to 8 feet during the future Phase III
development for long term flood mitigation As mentioned previously the majority
of the project site is underlain by compressible lagoonal estuarine deposits on the
order of about 7 to 40 feet thick Therefore placement of the substantial new fills to
raise the site to the future finished subgrade elevation likely will induce appreciable
ground settlements as a result of consolidation of the underlying compressible
deposits
Based on our engineering analyses we anticipate that ground settlements on the
order of about 10 to 20 inches may be anticipated as a result of the consolidation of
the compressible deposits under the future fill loads Due to the substantial
thickness and clayey nature of the compressible lagoonal estuarine deposits our
preliminary analyses suggest that 80 percent of the anticipated ground settlement
could take up to 5 to 7 years to occur To reduce the long settlement waiting
period we recommend considering a surcharge program with the installation of
wick drains during the Phase III site development
It should be recognized that it is very difficult to accurately predict the exact time
required for the filled ground to settle since the settlement rate is affected by
variations of the soil structure and the history of the soil deposition Therefore a
settlement monitoring program should be implemented during Phase III
construction as discussed in the following section
Settlement Monitoring
In general we recommend incorporating a settlement waiting period into the future
construction schedule The settlement waiting period should commence after
completion of the fill placement to the finished subgrade elevation or top of the
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 53
Hawaii California
surcharge fill if appropriate As indicated previously it is difficult to accurately
predict the exact time required for the filled ground to settle The estimated
settlement waiting period could vary by as much as 100 percent from the actual
settlement period for the soft loose lagoonal estuarine deposits encountered at the
project site Therefore the actual settlement rates should be monitored and a
settlement monitoring program should be established to evaluate the magnitude
and rate of the estimated settlements during the fill placement and settlement
waiting period In addition a contingency plan should be devised to accommodate
the potential delay in construction schedule that may be involved if a longer
settlement waiting period is required
To monitor the actual settlement rate we recommend installing settlement gauges
in the fill areas at selected locations across the project site The locations of the
settlement gauges should be determined when the grading plans for the Phase III
development is finalized A typical settlement gauge detail is provided on Plate 6
for reference A qualified professional surveyor should optically read the settlement
gauges and transmit the readings to the project geotechnical engineer for review in
a timely manner The settlement gauges should be established on the subgrade
soils prior to placement of the new fills We recommend taking two readings
24 hours apart for each settlement gauge prior to placement of the new fills to
establish a baseline Subsequent readings of the settlement gauges should be
taken on a bi weekly basis for the entire site filling and settlement waiting period
3 15 Excavation
Based on the current design concept we anticipate that excavations will be
needed for the construction of the below grade portion of the pump station building and
installation of utility lines at the project site Based on our field exploration excavations
for the project will encounter soft loose soil conditions and shallow groundwater table
Excavation Method
In general the contractor should determine the method and equipment to be used
for excavation subject to practical limits and safety considerations Based on our
field exploration the surface fill soils and soft loose lagoonal estuarine deposits
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 54
Hawaii California
encountered in the borings may be excavated with normal excavators and or
backhoes However hard ripping or special excavating methods may be required
to remove boulders present in the subsurface especially in areas in proximity to
Kahauiki Stream Therefore the contractor should make allowances for the
additional time and expense that may be required by the hard excavation
Excavation Support
Excavation for underground structures and installation of utility lines will need to be
adequately shored to reduce the potential for adjacent ground movement The
excavated materials should not be stockpiled adjacent to the planned excavation
within a horizontal distance equal to the depth of the excavation to reduce the
potential for ground movement The excavation support and shoring system used
are the responsibility of the contractor and must comply with all applicable safety
requirements
One possible method of shoring would be to use interlocking sheet pile shoring
Use of a sheet pile shoring system may also serve as a cut off wall to aid in the
dewatering operations which is further discussed in the Dewatering section of this
report We recommended that the sheet piles used for shoring the excavation be
left in place to aid in dewatering the excavation It should be noted that difficulties
may arise during installation of the interlocking sheet pile walls due to the potential
presence of boulders in the subsurface
The contractor should be made solely responsible for the adequacy and safety of
the shoring installation Therefore we recommend the contractor retain a qualified
geotechnical engineer to design and evaluate the shoring system used His her
representative who should be required to be continuously present on site during
excavation and construction work will have the best opportunity to promptly
observe changing conditions during construction such as unforeseen subsoils
unexpectedly high groundwater table inappropriate construction sequence or
techniques etc which may affect shoring stability However it must be noted that
some minor movements of the shoring system and the adjacent ground may still
occur due to changes in earth stresses during excavation Due to the complexity of
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 55
Hawaii California
the stress changes it is difficult to accurately estimate the magnitude of movement
The magnitude also depends greatly upon workmanship such as how quickly and
tightly the shoring and bracing supports are installed the subsoil conditions the
size of the excavation and the rate of excavation
It is important to realize that the excavation shoring should be installed properly and
as early as practical and that the adjacent ground should be continuously monitored
for cracks dips and or other indications of movements with instruments
Dewatering of excavations will be necessary where the existing groundwater
level is above the bottom of the proposed excavation such as the below grade portion
of the pump station building and for the utility line installation Therefore we
recommend including dewatering provisions in the contract documents for construction
Since the excavation will involve discharge of groundwater a National Pollutant
Discharge Elimination System NPDES permit may be necessary The contractor
should consult their independent consultant for the latest regulations and information
pertaining to site specific dewatering during construction
Dewatering Method
The contractor is responsible for dewatering for construction The selection of
equipment and methods of dewatering should be left up to the contractor and
he she should be aware that modifications to the dewatering system may be
required during construction depending on the conditions encountered
The dewatering method selected should have minimal impact on the groundwater
level surrounding the proposed excavation
It is our opinion that the definition of Dewatering in the contract documents should
be written to include all works or systems required to lower the natural groundwater
table and or to exclude the water from the excavations to allow construction of the
proposed structures under safe and dry conditions These works or systems may
include but are not limited to grouting cut off walls tremie concrete plugs or
combination of the above and or other possible methods Based on previous
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 56
Hawaii California
experience an interlocking sheet pile shoring system embedded into the stiff
alluvial soil deposits may work successfully in reducing the amount of seepage
water Therefore a sheet pile shoring system embedded into the alluvial deposits
should be considered for the construction cost estimate of this project
Dewatering Considerations
We suggest that the following three basic criteria be considered in selection of a
suitable method of dewatering
a
The dewatering method should result in the least disturbance or
damage to existing structures roads and environment
b
The dewatering method should maintain stability of and provide
safe and dry working conditions in the excavation
c
The dewatering method should be sufficiently flexible to allow
modifications to accommodate various ground conditions
Dewatering Precaution and Monitoring
The potential impact of the dewatering system selected on depressing the natural
groundwater table must be carefully evaluated by the contractor prior to dewatering
We recommend that the contractor retain a qualified geotechnical engineer to
design and evaluate the dewatering system used
The contractor should be solely responsible for the impact and safety of the
dewatering operations His her qualified representative who should be required to
be continuously present on site during dewatering activities will have the best
opportunity to promptly observe the effects of dewatering during construction and to
implement as soon as possible necessary precautionary or remedial measures
including but not limited to stopping or slowing down the dewatering operations
Where encountered at the bottom of excavations permeable granular subsoils may
be susceptible to piping and quick conditions The dewatering operations should
be carried out without creating a quick condition or softening at the excavation
bottoms Therefore the project dewatering operations should be performed without
pumping out soil fines pumping clear water only and should be coordinated with
shoring installation such that the excavation stability is not adversely affected
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 57
Hawaii California
Excessive pumping which removes soil fines may result in a blowing or heaving
of the excavation bottom or sides
Special caution should also be taken to avoid dewatering utility trenches connected
to excavations If this occurs the granular bedding and or backfill in the utility
trenches could act as subdrains and cause significant areal groundwater drawdown
resulting in settlements and potential damage to utility lines and or other adjacent
existing structures
3 17 New Sewer and Drain Lines
A new 18 inch diameter gravity sewer line hugging along the makai side of the
proposed flood wall will be installed from about the existing Kahauiki Makai Bridge to
near the northeastern corner of Building T 1522 Based on the information provided
the design pipe invert elevations will be up to about 8 feet below the existing ground
surface at the deepest In addition new sewer manholes will be installed at selected
locations along the new sewer line alignment We understand that new drain lines for
interior drainage are also planned for the project development
Based on our field exploration we anticipate that the majority of the new sewer
and drain lines will be underlain by stiff dense surface fill soils However the deeper
portions of these new utility lines may be underlain by the soft loose lagoonal estuarine
deposits below the surface fills as encountered in the drilled borings across the project
site Therefore special attention should be given to the bedding requirements and soft
ground stabilization measures as discussed in the following subsections Shoring and
dewatering of the planned excavations are anticipated in this area due to the soft
subsoil conditions and shallow groundwater table encountered Detailed discussions
and recommendations pertaining to shoring and dewatering requirements should be
referred to the Excavation and Dewatering sections herein
Earth Pressure Loads on Pipes
Loads on buried pipes are influenced by the width of the trench the size of the
pipes the unit weight of backfill material and the frictional resistance between the
backfill material and the trench walls To calculate the vertical loads on the buried
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 58
Hawaii California
sewer and drain pipes we recommend using an average unit weight of 110 pcf for
the backfill material and a coefficient of friction of 0 25 Earth forces upon the pipe
generally increase rapidly with the width of the trench Therefore the width of the
trench should be kept to a minimum Traffic loads on the buried pipes if applicable
should also be considered for the portions of the pipes located in roadway areas
Pipe Bedding
The stress distribution against the bottom of a pipe has a great effect upon the load
supporting capacity of the pipe Therefore pipe bedding is an important design
consideration In general we recommend using granular bedding consisting of
6 inches of free draining granular materials such as No 3B Fine gravel ASTM
C 33 No 67 gradation below the pipes and manhole structures located over
stiff dense soil conditions
We envision that soft loose lagoonal estuarine deposits may be encountered at or
near the invert elevations along some of the sewer and drain lines planned
Therefore we recommend providing a subgrade stabilization layer consisting of
18 to 24 inches of No 2 Rock ASTM C 33 No 4 gradation wrapped in a
non woven filter fabric Mirafi 180N or equivalent below the bedding layer for
uniform support The stabilization layer should extend beyond the sides of the pipe
a minimum width of one fourth the outside diameter of the pipe or 12 inches
whichever is greater A typical section of the trench detail is presented on Plate 7
for reference
In general we anticipate that utility lines with an invert elevation deeper than about
2 feet MSL would encounter the soft loose lagoonal estuarine deposits and will
likely require the use of the stabilization layer It should be noted that some of the
lagoonal estuarine deposits at the site are highly sensitive and may be subjected to
appreciable settlement due to disturbance caused by construction activities and
shoring installation and or extraction Therefore special care should be exercised
during the shoring installation and or extraction process
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 59
Hawaii California
Trench Backfill
In general free draining granular materials such as No 3B Fine gravel
ASTM C 33 No 67 gradation should be used for the initial trench backfill up to
about 12 inches above the pipes or 12 inches above the groundwater level It is
critical to use this free draining material to reduce the potential for formation of
voids below the haunches of the pipes and to provide adequate support for the
sides of the pipes Improper backfill material around the pipes and improper
placement of the backfill could result in backfill settlement and pipe damage Where
groundwater is encountered the bedding should be wrapped on all sides by
non woven filter fabric Mirafi 180N or equivalent
The upper portion of the trench backfill from a level of 12 inches above the pipes to
the top of the subgrade or finished grade may consist of the excavated granular
materials with a maximum particle size of 6 inches or select granular fill materials
The backfill material should be moisture conditioned to above the optimum
moisture content placed in maximum 8 inch level loose lifts and mechanically
compacted to at least 90 percent relative compaction to reduce the potential for
future ground subsidence In areas where trenches will be in paved areas the
upper 3 feet of the trench backfill below the pavement finish grade should be
compacted to no less than 95 percent relative compaction Relative compaction
refers to the in place dry density of soil expressed as a percentage of the maximum
dry density as determined by ASTM Test Designation D 1557 91 Optimum
moisture is the water content percentage by weight corresponding to the
maximum dry density
In order to reduce the potential for pavement distress resulting from the settlement
of utility trench backfill a temporary pavement section may be considered at the
completion of the trench work A permanent pavement section may be placed after
the backfilled area has come to equilibrium under backfill earth loads
Precautions should be taken against the occurrence of pipeline flotation before and
during trench backfilling due to possible influx of large quantities of groundwater
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 60
Hawaii California
into the trenches The buoyant uplift forces due to groundwater influx may lift
empty or even partially water filled pipes
Pipe Settlement
Primary settlement of the new pipe installation is generally caused by the difference
in the unit weight of the lighter excavated original earth and the heavier compacted
backfill material placed over the pipeline The net increase in loading may cause
settlement of the underlying subsoils below the trench invert Based on our
exploration and analyses small primary settlements on the order of about 1 inch
may be anticipated for the new sewer and drain line alignments underlain by the
stiff dense surface fill soils If soft loose soils are encountered at or near the pipe
invert elevation additional settlement on the order of 1 to 2 inches may occur
during construction due to disturbance of the soft soils and vibration due to the
installation and removal of the sheet pile shoring This is further discussed in the
Construction Considerations subsection herein
Manhole Structures
In general we recommend that the bottom of the new manhole structures bear on
6 inches of open graded gravel ASTM C 33 No 67 gradation placed over the
stiff dense surface fills anticipated at the bottom elevation of the new manhole
structures If soft and or loose soils are encountered at the bottom of the new
manhole structures we recommend providing a minimum of 2 feet of No 3B Fine
gravel ASTM C 33 No 67 gradation wrapped in a filter fabric Mirafi 180N or
equivalent over the in situ soft and or loose lagoonal estuarine deposits In lieu of
the No 3B Fine gravel the stabilization layer may consist of No 2 Rock that meets
the requirements of Section 15 of the City and County Standard Specifications
Based on our engineering analyses it is our opinion that the net increase in bearing
pressure on the underlying soil deposits resulting from the manhole construction
would be relatively small We expect settlements on the order of less than 1 inch for
these structures bearing on stiff dense soil conditions We anticipate settlements on
the order of less than 2 inches for these structures bearing on the soft soil
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 61
Hawaii California
stabilization layer for the soft soil conditions The majority of these settlements will
likely occur during construction before connection with the piping is made
The lateral earth pressures acting on the proposed underground manhole
structures will depend on the type of backfill used the extent of backfill and the
compaction effort on the backfill materials around the structures Therefore we
recommend using granular backfill materials as described below around the
structure to reduce the compaction effort required which may cause additional
lateral earth pressures We recommend designing the new manhole structures to
resist the following lateral earth pressures at rest conditions from the adjacent
soils

Surcharge stresses due to areal surcharges traffic loads line loads and point

Lateral loads acting on the structures may be resisted by friction developed

foundation system A coefficient of friction of 0 45 may be used between the base

In order to resist hydrostatic uplift pressures the dead weight of the structure the
expected minimum weight of the contained fluid and the backfill could be used to

developed from adhesion between the concrete walls and the adjacent soils When
evaluating the resistance to uplift loads a total unit weight of 110 pounds per cubic
foot buoyant unit weight and an adhesion value of 100 pounds per
square foot psf uniform distribution may be used for design based on the open
graded gravel backfill material
Backfilling of Manhole Excavations
The manhole excavations will need to be properly backfilled If backfilling below the
groundwater level is necessary we recommend using No 2 Rock ASTM C 33
No 4 gradation from the bottom of the manholes up to an elevation of about the
high groundwater level The first 12 inches of backfill above the No 2 Rock should
consist of No 3B Fine gravel ASTM C 33 No 67 gradation A layer of filter fabric
such as Mirafi 180 N or equivalent should be provided around the No 3B Fine
gravel and No 2 Rock to reduce the potential for migration of fines from the
surrounding soils into the open graded gravel and rock fill The excavated on site
soils excluding the soft and wet soils may be used as backfill above the filter fabric
up to the finish grades
The soil backfill above the No 3B Fine gravel should be placed in thin lifts normally
8 inches in loose lift thickness with each lift mechanically compacted to a minimum
of 90 percent relative compaction Relative compaction refers to the in place dry
density of soil expressed as a percentage of the maximum dry density of the same
soil determined in accordance with ASTM Test Designation D 1557 91
Construction Considerations
The settlement estimates presented in the Pipe Settlement subsection assume
that proper construction procedures and good workmanship will be consistently
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 63
Hawaii California
practiced by the contractor during pipeline installation operations Based on our
knowledge and past experience with similar soils significant settlement of the pipes
may be attributed to the construction methodology and equipment used by the
contractor Therefore special attention should be given to the installation
procedure for the proposed new sewer and drain lines especially in soft soil
conditions to reduce the potential for settlement distress in the future
As previously recommended the sewer drain pipes and manhole structures over
soft soils should be supported by approximately 6 inches of No 3B Fine gravel
bedding layer over 24 inches of free draining No 2 Rock wrapped in a non woven
filter fabric The filter fabric is used to provide separation between the coarse
aggregate No 2 Rock and the fine grained soil soft clays In general a
minimum overlap of 2 feet should be provided between the ends of each roll of the
filter fabric placed along the pipe alignment under dry conditions If the filter fabric
is not properly overlapped it is possible that the gravel placed may migrate through
the openings in the filter fabric and mixed with the underlying soft soils This may
result in settlement of the sewer drain pipe due to loss of cushion materials into the
soft subsoils
Since the construction below the pipe invert may be performed in wet conditions
we envision that it would be difficult to observe the fabric installation process below
the groundwater level In addition we believe that it would be difficult for the
contractor to assure that the proper minimum overlap is maintained Therefore we
believe that if placement of the filter fabric in wet conditions is necessary the
seams of the fabric should be sewn to provide a higher assurance that gaps will not
occur in the filter fabric As a result we recommend that sewing the seams of the
filter fabric be incorporated into the construction procedure to reduce the potential
for large scale settlements of the sewer drain pipes
Due to the soft loose soil conditions anticipated at some of the pipe invert elevation
care should also be exercised during the backfilling operations of the trench
excavation Heavy equipment and vibratory action of the compactor may exert high
pressures onto the pipe and supporting soils during the trench backfilling
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 64
Hawaii California
operations resulting in potential settlement of the soft clays and pipe during
construction Therefore the size of the equipment used to compact the backfill
around and above the pipe should to be limited to less than 4 tons in weight
Since the in situ soft clays is considered to be highly sensitive i e the clay may
settle when disturbed or remolded during construction installation of the new
sewer drain pipe may be subjected to some amount of settlement due to
disturbance of the soft soils The magnitude of settlement will depend on the type
of construction equipment and level of care taken during construction We
speculate that this type of settlement may be on the order of less than 1 to 2 inches
assuming that small equipment is used to compact the backfill around and above
the pipe and that extra care is exercised during construction In addition care
should be exercised during the removal of the sheet pile shoring since the
vibrations generated may cause potential pipeline settlement
3 18 Pavement Design
Based on the information provided we understand that the sections of Annex
Road and Loop Road adjacent to the new detention basin will be graded with fill
materials and paved with new asphalt pavements We have assumed that the fill
materials needed to raise the roadway grades will have a minimum CBR value of 20 In
addition we understand that the new pavements will be subjected to a maximum
vehicle load of up to 80 tons corresponding to a Traffic Category of VII Based on the
Road Class type of road street and Traffic Category traffic composition information
envisioned for the new pavement areas a Design Index DI of 10 was determined for
our pavement analyses
The pavement analyses were performed in general accordance with the Unified
Facilities Criteria and the Army s pavement design
software Pavement Transportation Computer Assisted Structural Engineering
PCASE Based on our pavement analyses we recommend the following design
pavement section for the new sections of Annex Road and Loop Road
SECTION 3 DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
Page 65
Hawaii California
Design Flexible Pavement Section
4 0 inch Asphaltic Concrete
6 0 inch Aggregate Base Course 100 Percent Relative Compaction
10 0 inch Total Pavement Thickness over Moist Compacted Subgrade
In general the pavement subgrades should be scarified to a depth of about
8 inches moisture conditioned to above the optimum moisture and recompacted to a
minimum of 95 percent relative compaction Relative compaction refers to the in place
dry density of soil expressed as a percentage of the maximum dry density of the same soil
established in accordance with ASTM D 1557 Optimum moisture is the water content
percentage by dry weight corresponding to the maximum dry density The aggregate
base course should consist of crushed basaltic aggregates compacted to not less than
100 percent relative compaction CBR and field density tests should be performed on
the actual subgrade soils encountered during construction to confirm the adequacy of
the above section
Paved areas should be sloped and drainage gradients should be maintained to
carry surface water off site Surface water ponding should not be allowed on site during
or after construction Where concrete curbs are used to isolate landscaping in or
adjacent to the pavement areas we recommend that the curbs extend a minimum of
2 inches into the subgrade soil below the aggregate base course layer to reduce the
potential for migration of excessive landscape water into the pavement section

forwarded to Geolabs for review and written comments prior to construction This review

3 20 Post Design Services Services During Construction
It is highly recommended to retain Geolabs for geotechnical engineering support
and continued services during construction The following are critical items of
construction monitoring that require Special Inspection
Review of the pile driving equipment
Review of pile load test results
Observation of test pile and production pile installation
Observation of sheet pile installation
Observation of shallow footing excavation and preparation
Observation of the subgrade soil preparation
Observation of fill backfill placement and compaction
Review of shoring and dewatering submittal
A Geolabs representative should monitor other aspects of the earthwork
construction to observe compliance with the intent of the design concepts
specifications or recommendations and to expedite suggestions for design changes
that may be required in the event that subsurface conditions differ from those
anticipated at the time this report was prepared The recommendations provided herein
are contingent upon such observations
We understand that Geolabs may not be retained to provide on site construction
observation during the foundation and earthwork operations Therefore we recommend
retaining a competent geotechnical engineer with a minimum of 10 years experience in
construction observation and testing of earthwork operations during the project
construction

SECTION 4 LIMITATIONS
The analyses and recommendations submitted herein are based in part upon
information obtained from field data points Variations of the subsurface soil conditions
between and beyond the field data points may occur and the nature and extent of these
variations may not become evident until construction is underway If variations then
appear evident it will be necessary to re evaluate the recommendations provided
herein
This report has been prepared for the exclusive use of Sato Associates Inc
and their client Department of the Army US Army Corps of Engineers for specific
application to the 56024 Flood Mitigation Structures project at
Fort Shafter Flats in accordance with generally accepted geotechnical engineering
principles and practices No warranty is expressed or implied
This report has been prepared solely for the purpose of assisting the architect
and engineers in the design of the proposed project Therefore this report may not
contain sufficient data or the proper information to serve as the basis for preparation of
construction cost estimates
The owner client should be aware that unanticipated subsurface conditions are
commonly encountered Unforeseen subsurface conditions such as perched
groundwater soft deposits hard layers or loose fills may occur in localized areas and
may require additional probing or corrections in the field which may result in
construction delays to attain a properly constructed project Therefore a sufficient
contingency fund is recommended to accommodate these possible extra costs

A P P E N D I X A
Field Exploration
We explored the subsurface conditions by drilling and sampling 25 borings
designated as Boring Nos 101 through 129 excluding and 113 to depths
of about 16 5 to 102 5 feet below the existing ground surface at the approximate locations
shown on the Boring Location Plan Plate 3 We used a combination of 4 inch diameter
continuous flight solid stem augers and continued using PQ size wireline coring tools to
advance the PQ rods as rotary wash casing The boreholes were advanced utilizing the
PQ casing only as a rotary wash drilling method therefore there were no soil samples
retrieved between the soil sampling points
Our geologist classified the materials encountered in the borings by visual and
textural examination in the field He monitored the drilling operations on a near continuous
basis These classifications were further reviewed visually and by laboratory testing Soils
were classified in general conformance with the Unified Soil Classification System as
shown on the Key to Symbols Plate A Graphic representations of the materials
encountered are provided on the Logs of Borings Plates A 1 through A 25
Sampling of the soils was performed using the Standard Penetration Test SPT
split
spoon
sampler
ASTM D 1586
and
the
modified
California
sampler
ASTM D 3550 In the softer fine grained soils undisturbed samples were obtained by
using thin walled tube samplers or Shelby Tubes ASTM D 1587
In situ testing of the subsurface materials in the borings included the SPT which
was performed in accordance with ASTM D 1586 SPT sampling provides a measure of
the resistance or consistency of a soil and is reported as the uncorrected N value Nf
which is defined as the number of blows required to drive a standard split spoon
sampler 12 inches with a 140 lb hammer after 6 inches of initial seating The
penetration resistance of the modified California sampler was recorded in a similar
manner and the modified California sampler blows per 12 inches were converted to Nf
using an empirical factor of 0 55
The uncorrected Nf values were then converted to N60 values using a factor of
1 31 obtained by calibration of the automatic drop hammer on the rig used for the field
exploration Both the Nf and N60 values are shown on the Logs of Borings at the
appropriate sample depths The hydraulic pressure required to advance the thin walled
samplers is also indicated on the Logs at the appropriate sample depths

APPENDIX B
W O 6311 00 D
GEOLABS INC
AUGUST 2011 Page B 1
Hawaii California
A P P E N D I X B
Laboratory Tests
Moisture Content ASTM D 2216 and Unit Weight determinations ASTM D 2937
were performed on selected soil samples as an aid in the classification and evaluation of
soil properties The test results are presented on the Logs of Borings at the appropriate
sample depths
Fifty four 54 Atterberg Limits tests ASTM D 4318 were performed on selected
soil samples to evaluate the liquid and plastic limits and to aid in soil classification The
test results are summarized on the Logs of Borings at the appropriate sample depths
The test results are also provided on Plates B 1 through B 6
Forty eight 48 Sieve Analysis Hydrometer tests ASTM C 117 C 136 and
D 422 were performed on selected soil samples to evaluate the gradation
characteristics of the soils and to aid in soil classification Graphic presentations of the
grain size distributions are provided on Plates B 7 through B 16
Twelve 12 Consolidation tests ASTM D 2435 were performed on selected soil
samples to evaluate the compressibility characteristics of the on site soils The test
results are plotted on Plates B 17 through B 28
Sixteen 16 Direct Shear tests ASTM D 3080 were performed on selected
samples to evaluate the shear strength characteristics of the materials tested The test
results are presented on Plates B 29 through B 44
To evaluate the undrained shear strength of the clayey soils thirty five 35
Unconsolidated Undrained Triaxial Compression tests were performed on selected
in situ soil samples in accordance with ASTM D 2850 The approximate in situ effective
overburden pressure was used as the applied confining pressure for the relatively
undisturbed soil sample The test results and the stress strain curves are presented on
Plates B 45 through B 79
To evaluate the undrained shear strength of the clayey soils three 3
Consolidated Undrained Triaxial Compression tests were performed on selected in situ
soil samples in accordance with ASTM D 4767 The test results and the stress strain
curves at different confining pressures are presented on Plates B 80 through B 82
To assist in evaluating the corrosion potential of the on site soils pH ASTM G
51 and minimum resistivity ASTM G 57 were performed on eight 8 selected samples
of soil The test results are presented on Plates B 83 and B 84
To evaluate the permeability of soils encountered at the site seven 7 Hydraulic
Conductivity of Saturated Porous Materials by Flexible Wall Permeameter tests
ASTM D 5084 were performed on selected samples of the on site materials The test
results are presented on Plates B 85 thru B 91

APPENDIX B 1
Pacific Geotechnical Engineers Inc Laboratory Testing

B 1
APPENDIX B
LABORATORY TESTING
GENERAL To evaluate their engineering properties select soil samples obtained during the
field exploration were subjected to laboratory moisture content and dry density determinations
Atterberg Limits tests gradation tests consolidation tests moisture density relations tests
California Bearing Ratio tests strength tests specific gravity tests and permeability tests The
tests and their results are described in the following paragraphs
MOISTURE CONTENT AND DRY DENSITY Relatively undisturbed selected soil samples
were tested to measure their in situ moisture contents and dry densities The tests were
performed in general accordance with ASTM D 2216 test method Results of the moisture
content and dry density determinations are presented on the Logs of Borings for land L 1
overwater borings W 1 through W 10 at the respective sample depths
ATTERBERG LIMITS Twenty six 26 conventional not dried and seven 7 organic
oven dried Atterberg Limits tests were performed on select samples in general accordance with
ASTM D4318 test method The results of all of these tests are presented on Plates B 1 1 through
B 1 6 The organic Atterberg Limits test results are summarized in Table B 1
GRADATION ANALYSIS Thirty five 35 gradation analysis tests were performed in
general accordance with ASTM D 422 to evaluate grain size distribution The test results are
CONSOLIDATION Fifteen 15 samples of elastic silt and clay were tested in general
accordance with ASTM D2435 test procedure to determine their compressibility characteristics
MOISTURE DENSITY RELATIONS Ten 10 moisture density relations tests were
performed on bulk samples of near surface soils in general accordance with ASTM D 1557 test
Flood Mitigation Structures
PGE Job No 1875 028
Pacific Geotechnical
Engineers Inc
B 2
CALIFORNIA BEARING RATIO CBR Ten 10 single point laboratory CBR tests were
performed on the bulk samples used in the moisture density relations tests in general accordance
with ASTM D 1883 test method The results of the CBR tests are presented on Plates B 5 1
through B 5 10
SHEAR STRENGTH TX UU Twenty six 26 shear strength tests were performed on
relatively undisturbed soil sample to evaluate their shear strength properties The triaxial tests
were performed under unconsolidated undrained triaxial TX UU conditions in general
accordance with ASTM D2850 test method The tests were performed on soils samples at their
field moisture contents Total stress properties were measured in these tests The results of the
strength tests are summarized in Table B 2
SHEAR STRENGTH TX CUpp Five 5 shear strength tests were performed on relatively
undisturbed soil sample to evaluate their shear strength properties The triaxial tests were
performed under consolidated undrained conditions with pore pressure measurements
TX CUpp conditions in general accordance with ASTM D4767 test method The tests were
performed on soils samples at their field moisture contents Total stress and effective stress
SPECIFIC GRAVITY TESTS Eleven 11 specific gravity tests were performed on soil
sample to determine their specific gravities The tests were performed in general accordance
with ASTM D854 test method The results of the specific gravity tests are summarized in Table
B 3
PERMEABILITY TESTS Ten 10 permeability tests were performed on soil samples to
determine their permeability coefficients k The tests were performed in general accordance
with ASTM D5084 test method The results of the permeability tests are summarized in Table
B 4

REPORT FOR THE GEOPHYSICAL SURVEYS AT FORT
SHAFTER FLATS OAHU HAWAII
This letter report presents the results of the geophysical surveys performed by Global
Geophysics in February 2011 The geophysical surveys were carried out in support of
the geotechnical engineering exploration for 56024 Flood Mitigation
Structures Fort Shafter Flats Oahu Hawaii The objective of the investigation is to
determine the depth to bedrock below the site The surveys were centered around an H
shaped building Building T 1507
1
GEOPHYSICAL METHODS AND FIELD PROCEDURES
Seismic reflection was initially proposed and carried out on the first day However the
reflected seismic signal was weak below 150 ft The reason was that the excavator could
not hit the ground hard enough due to the pressure regulator Electrical resistivity
tomography was used only on one transect due to the limitation on the open space 1600
2200 straight line was required Therefore gravity survey was selected to complete the
investigation The following paragraphs describe the methods and field procedures
1 1
Seismic reflection
The seismic reflection technique maps the subsurface stratigraphy based on density and
velocity contrasts between earth materials The seismic wave generated at the ground
surface travels through the earth and is reflected an interfaces where a change in density
and velocity occurs The reflected waves are detected by a geophone array and recorded
by a seismograph
The seismic reflection survey was conducted using two Geometric Geode 24 channel
digital seismographs with roll along switch box The sensors were Mark Products 14 Hz
vertical geophones and the seismic energy source was excavator bucket A pilot test with
different charge sizes and offsets was conducted to determine the optimal field data
collecting parameters Field procedures consisted of laying out the geophone cables and
March 24 2011
Fort Shafter Flats
2
Global Geophysics
the geophones The data was examined in the field for quality control and then stored
digitally for later processing The post survey processing consisted of downloading the
data performing additional editing and processing and producing interpreted geologic
sections
1 2
Electrical Resistivity Tomography ERT
The electrical resistivity tomography technique maps differences in the electrical
properties of geologic materials These differences can result from variations in
lithology water content and pore water chemistry The method involves transmitting an
electric current into the ground between two electrodes and measuring the voltage
between two other electrodes The direct measurement is an apparent resistivity of the
area beneath the electrodes that includes deeper layers as the electrode spacing is
increased Recent advances in technology permit rapid collection of multiple soundings
using up to 112 electrodes for each spread The data are modeled to create a 2 D geo
electric cross section that is useful for mapping both vertical and horizontal variations of
the subsurface strata
The data were acquired with an using up to 56 electrodes spaced at a
20 feet interval Once the electrode array was installed in the ground multiple soundings
were automatically carried out by the control unit Downloading and routine modeling of
the data was done on site to provide preliminary analysis and QA QC of the data These
results were displayed on a color monitor as cross section that highlight changes in
resistivity with depth along the transect
1 3
Gravity
The gravity instrument measures the earth s gravitational acceleration After corrections
are made to the gravity measurements for latitude elevation tide and terrain of each
gravity station the gravity values represents variations or excess and differences in mass
of the subsurface geology
The gravity measurements were made with a Burris digital gravity meter that has a
reading resolution of and a standard deviation of less than 10 µgals
The latitude longitude and elevation of stations in the courtyards were obtained by
contract surveyors Control Point Surveying
Before taking measurements at the site the gravity meter was leveled energized and
stabilized for about 4 hours before taken to the site Thereafter the instrument was
transported to each measurement station leveled and stabilized for 3 minutes or longer
before taking a set of readings The gravity meter was returned to a calibration station
several times during the day to monitor for signs of instrument drift
Data were recorded in the field input to computer after the survey and subsequently
corrected for latitude elevation drift tide and terrain The computer program
GravMaster was used to process the gravity data
March 24 2011
Fort Shafter Flats
3
Global Geophysics
2
DATA PROCESSING AND RESULTS
The locations of the geophysical lines and gravity stations are shown in Figure 1 The
locations of the gravity model profiles are also presented in Figure 1
The seismic reflection profile is presented in Figure 2 No strong reflectors are shown
below 150 ft due to weak seismic source The marsh deposit estuarine deposit lagoonal
deposit with thickness varying between 10 and 60 ft is not resolved with this reflection
geophone array setup The same data set was re processed to obtain the s wave profile
The s wave velocity varies between 500 ft s and 1800 ft s
The resistivity profile is presented in Figure 3 The conductive zone approximately 295 ft
below ground surface located between Stations 300 ft and 400 ft suggests that the areas
with resistivity greater than 5 ohm m are not basal bedrock That means no bedrock is
encountered 340 ft below ground surface at this location
Gravity readings were taken at 22 stations with a couple of readings on the bedrock
After tide free air latitude drift Bougeur and terrain corrections were applied to the
gravity readings the gravity data are modeled along 6 transects The Bougeur gravity and
model profiles are presented in Figure 4 The densities of 1 7 g cm3 for the overburden
and 2 6 g cm3 for the basal bedrock are used for the modeling The depth and elevation
contour plans of the modeled bedrock surface are shown in Figure 5 The depth to
modeled bedrock surface varies between 160 ft and 480 ft
CLOSURE
Global Geophysics services will be conducted in a manner consistent with the level of
care and skill ordinarily exercised by other members of the geophysical community
currently practicing under similar conditions subject to the time limits and financial and
physical constraints applicable to the services However seismic reflection ERT and
gravity are remote sensing geophysical methods that may not detect all subsurface
conditions such as velocity and thickness variations Furthermore the modeled depths to
bedrock may be revised accurate density information becoming available In general the
errors in the interpreted depths dependent on the resolution of the technique are
estimated to be approximately 15 of the true depths
We appreciate the opportunity to work with you on this project and we hope that you
find the results of the geophysical survey useful to your investigation If you have any
questions regarding this report please call the undersigned at We look
forward to providing you with additional geophysical services in the future
Sincerely
Global Geophysics

EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
A nondestructive evaluation NDE investigation was conducted on 14 precast concrete
pile foundations and one abutment pile for a bridge in Fort Shafter Hawaii The field
investigation was performed using the Parallel Seismic PS and Sonic Echo Impulse Response
SE IR nondestructive test methods The investigation was performed to determine the length
and condition of the driven piles
The NDE results indicate the concrete piles varied in length from approximately 55 7
79 1 feet measured from the bottom of the deck A summary of all test results is presented in
Table I in Section 3 0 The reported pile lengths are measured from the bottom of the bridge
deck to the tip of the pile There were no significant defects observed within the piles bases
upon the SE IR test data The PS testing indicates that the compressional wave velocity of the
piles is approximately sec which is typical of precast concrete driven piles Therefore
a compressional wave velocity of sec was assumed during the SE IR data analysis
The compressional wave velocity likely varies slightly from pile to pile and may be the source of
the margin of error of SE IR test results
Olson Job No 3523A
Page 2
2 0 PROJECT BACKGROUND AND INVESTIGATION OVERVIEW
A nondestructive evaluation NDE investigation was conducted on the concrete driven
pile foundations for a bridge in Fort Shafter Hawaii The field investigation was performed
using the Parallel Seismic PS and Sonic Echo Impulse Response SE IR nondestructive test
methods The investigation was performed to determine the length and condition of the driven
piles The field investigation was conducted on March 28th 2011 by Mr Matt Hergert Project
Engineer of Olson Engineering with assistance from GeoLabs Inc personnel The results of all
testing are presented herein
Parallel Seismic PS The PS test method see Section 4 2 was used to determine the length of
a single pile on the west abutment The PS method involves installing a boring near the
unknown foundation typically at least 10 to 15 feet beyond the expected foundation
depth A hydrophone receiver is lowered into the borehole at 1 foot increments and the
foundation element is struck with an instrumented hammer A compressive wave travels through
the foundation and soil to the receiver By stacking records at multiple depths a change in the
wave front of the data is observed at the pile tip and therefore the length of the foundation can
be determined The PS performed on the west abutment pile showed that the pile has a length of
measured from ground level
Sonic Echo and Impulse Response SE IR The SE IR test method see Section 4 1 is used to
determine the length and condition of unknown drilled shafts or driven pile foundations The
method can detect anomalies in the piles such as cracks bulbs or necks The method involves
striking the foundation in this case on the column above the pile with a 3 lb instrumented
hammer and measuring the vibration of the foundation with a receiver Compressional wave
echoes and resonances from the pile tip are observed in the vibration data in both the time and
frequency domains and relate to the length and condition of the pile The SE IR tests performed
on 14 piles showed that the lengths of the tested piles varied from 1 ft measured from
the bottom of the bridge deck

The SE IR test was performed on each of the 14 piles All data from the SE IR testing
was also clear high quality data All of the piles tested displayed a distinct bottom echo The
SE IR test results showed that all the tested piles are sound with no major anomalies cracks
identified
One PS test was performed on a pile of the west abutment The PS data sets collected on
the pile provided clear high quality data Figure 2 presents an example PS data set The
compressive wave traveling down the pile is observed in the upper portion of the plot The slope
of the compressive wave front is the compressive wave speed here it is approximately equal to
sec which is a typical compressive wave speed for precast higher quality concrete
piles Below the tip of the pile the increasing distance through soil delays the compressive wave

pile in this case 41 3 feet from the top of the PS tube Note that the stickup length is 1 ft

NONDESTRUCTIVE TEST METHOD DESCRIPTIONS
The SE IR and PS nondestructive test methods are discussed below in Sections 4 1 and
4 2 respectively
4 1
Sonic Echo and Impulse Response Test Method
The SE method is a low strain integrity
test conducted from the top or side of the shaft
as shown in Figure 4 Test equipment
included a 3 lb impulse hammer a receiver
accelerometer mounted on the exposed side
of
the
pile
and
a
PC based
data
acquisition analysis system The impulse
hammer has a built in load cell that can
measure the force and duration of the impact
The test involves hitting the foundation top
with the hammer to generate energy that
travels to the bottom of the foundation The
wave reflects off irregularities cracks necks
bulbs soil intrusions voids etc and or the
bottom of the foundation and travels back
along the foundation to the top The receiver measures the vibration response of the foundation
to each impact The signal analyzer processes and displays the hammer and receiver outputs
Foundation length and integrity of concrete are evaluated by identifying and analyzing the arrival
times direction and amplitude of reflections measured by the receivers in time The echo depth
D is calculated by multiplying the reflection time t by the compression wave velocity V and
dividing this quantity by 2 to account for the fact that the wave has gone down and reflected back
i e D V t 2
Impulse Response IR Test Method The IR method is also an echo test and uses the
same test equipment as the SE method The test procedures are similar to the SE test procedures
Olson Job No 3523A
Page 8
but the data processing is different The IR method involves frequency domain data processing
i e the vibrations of the foundation measured by the receivers are processed with Fast Fourier
Transform FFT algorithms to generate transfer functions for analyses The coherence of the
impulse hammer impact and accelerometer receiver response data versus frequency is calculated
to indicate the data quality A coherence near 1 0 indicates good quality data For shafts in air or
in relatively soft soils the coherence will typically only be near 1 0 at frequencies for which the
mobility is non zero In the IR records the linear transfer function amplitude is in
inches second pound force on the vertical axis mobility and frequency in Hz on the horizontal
axis Because of the rod like shape of a deep foundation reflections are indicated by equally
spaced resonant peaks that correspond to modes of vibration associated with the depth of the
reflector The inverse of the SE reflection time t is equal to the change in frequency f
between the resonant peaks in the IR mobility plot The reflector depth is then calculated as
D V 2 f
SE IR Analyses Analysis of the length determination and the integrity evaluation of a
foundation for both the SE and IR methods is based on the identification and evaluation of
reflections However test results are analyzed in the time domain for the SE and in the
frequency domain for the IR method The reflections are shown as resonant frequency peaks in
the frequency domain for IR test data The two methods complement each other because the
identifications of reflections are sometimes clearer in either the time or the frequency domain In
this case reflections were clear in the time domain therefore only SE example data is presented
The SE and IR test methods are sensitive to changes in the shaft impedance shaft
concrete area velocity mass density where mass density equals unit weight divided by
gravity which cause the reflections of the compression wave energy Compression wave
energy hammer impact energy reflects differently from increased shaft impedance than from
decreased shaft impedance This phenomenon allows the type of reflector to be identified as
follows Soil intrusions honeycomb breaks cracks cold joints poor quality concrete and
similar defects referred to herein as a neck are identified as reflections that correspond to a
decrease in the shaft impedance Increases in the shaft cross section or the competency of
surrounding materials such as bedrock and stiffer soil strata referred to herein as a bulb are
Olson Job No 3523A
Page 9
identified as reflections corresponding to increases in the shaft impedance A decrease in
impedance is indicated by a downward initial break of a reflection event in an SE record and
frequency peaks positioned in a record such that a peak could be extrapolated to be near 0 Hz in
the mobility plot Conversely an increase in shaft impedance is identified by an upward initial
break for an SE reflector and frequency peaks positioned in an IR record such that a trough could
be extrapolated to be near 0 Hz in the mobility plot
When embedded length to diameter ratios exceed 20 1 to 30 1 for shafts in stiffer soils bedrock
the attenuation of compression wave energy is high and bottom echoes are weak or
unidentifiable in SE IR test results The term weak bottom echo is used to indicate that a
bottom echo is seen but that it is barely visible above the normal background noise Note that it
is possible for a perfectly sound shaft to have a weak bottom echo as a weak echo can be caused
by either a shallow reflector blocking energy from the shaft bottom or from wave energy
coupling into the bedrock at the shaft bottom rather than reflecting back up Thus the strength
of the bottom echo is used as a secondary minor consideration as to shaft condition

Parallel Seismic Test Method
The Parallel Seismic PS method is used to nondestructively evaluate NDE the depth
of unknown foundations The PS test equipment used in this investigation included a 3 lb
instrumented hammer single hydrophone receiver and a dynamic signal analyzer Olson
Instruments Freedom Data PC When the instrumented hammer impacts the foundation system
it triggers the PC based signal analyzer to capture time records of the vibrations received by the
hydrophone A National Instruments digital data acquisition card was used to acquire the data in
an Olson Instruments portable Freedom Data PC
The PS method see Figure 5 involves impacting the exposed portion of the foundation
or substructure attached to the foundation or a location which when impacted couples sufficient
energy to the pile or shaft to generate a sound or stress wave which travels down the foundation
The wave energy was tracked by a hydrophone receiver suspended in a water filled cased
borehole Boreholes are typically installed within 5 10 feet of the foundation system The PS
tests typically involve lowering the hydrophone s to the bottom of the borehole impacting the
exposed portion of the foundation structure and recording the hydrophone s responses The
hydrophone receiver s is then raised to the next test elevation increments of 1 or 2 feet are
typical This test sequence is repeated until the top of the casing or the top of the water level in
the casing is reached The pile depth is determined by plotting the hydrophone s response from
all depths on a single display For soils of constant velocity surrounding the piles a break in the
slope of the line occurs below the bottom of the piles indicating the pile depth For soils with
varying velocities a break often cannot be identified from the slope of the lines but the bottom
of the piles can be identified by observing the traces of the hydrophone plot to identify changes
in the response such as a reduction in signal amplitude change in signal frequency or
diffraction reflection of tube wave energy from the tips of piles diffraction is frequently the
indicator for the pile tip depth of steel sheet pilings
